Task instruction sent to agent 
# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes API Server Admission Webhook Chain

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the API server admission webhook chain: the webhook admission controller, the webhook call dispatch, and the admission response aggregation.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the domain domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

70-assistanttext-
I've successfully identified and documented all the Go source files implementing the Kubernetes API server admission webhook chain. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Components Found:

**1. Core Webhook Framework** (generic/):
- `webhook.go` - Main generic webhook handler that orchestrates the entire chain
- `interfaces.go` - Defines Dispatcher, Source, and WebhookInvocation interfaces

**2. Mutating Webhooks** (mutating/):
- `plugin.go` - Plugin registration and Admit() entry point
- `dispatcher.go` - Core logic for invoking mutating webhooks with patch application
- `reinvocationcontext.go` - Handles reinvocation of webhooks when mutations occur

**3. Validating Webhooks** (validating/):
- `plugin.go` - Plugin registration and Validate() entry point
- `dispatcher.go` - Parallel execution of validating webhooks with response aggregation

**4. Webhook Configuration** (configuration/):
- `mutating_webhook_manager.go` - Manages MutatingWebhookConfiguration resources
- `validating_webhook_manager.go` - Manages ValidatingWebhookConfiguration resources

**5. Webhook Access & Request/Response** (accessors.go, request/admissionreview.go):
- `accessors.go` - WebhookAccessor interface providing unified access to webhook configs
- `admissionreview.go` - Creates and validates AdmissionReview objects for webhook communication

**6. Supporting Components**:
- `errors/statuserror.go` - Converts webhook rejections to API errors
- Predicate matchers for namespace, object, and rule-based filtering

The admission webhook chain follows this flow:
1. **Dispatch** → **ShouldCallHook** → Webhook matching
2. **Mutating webhooks**: Sequential execution with patch aggregation and reinvocation
3. **Validating webhooks**: Parallel execution with error aggregation
4. Response handling via *
... (truncated)

admission webhook chain is implemented across multiple Go packages that work together to handle dynamic admission control for API requests. The chain begins with the main Webhook handler in generic/webhook.go, which implements the core admission.Interface and orchestrates the entire webhook admission flow. When a request arrives, the Dispatch() method in generic/webhook.go coordinates with ShouldCallHook() to determine which webhooks should be invoked based on namespace selectors, object selectors, and resource rules. The actual webhook invocations are delegated to specialized Dispatcher implementations in the mutating and validating subpackages. For mutating webhooks, the mutatingDispatcher in mutating/dispatcher.go iterates through eligible webhooks and calls callAttrMutatingHook() for each one, which handles the HTTP request/response cycle, patch application, and reinvocation logic for consecutive mutations. The validatingDispatcher in validating/dispatcher.go runs validating webhooks in parallel (via goroutines) and aggregates their responses. Both dispatchers use the request/admissionreview.go utilities to create AdmissionReview objects via CreateAdmissionObjects() and validate responses via VerifyAdmissionResponse(). The WebhookAccessor interface (defined in accessors.go) provides a unified way to access webhook configuration details for both MutatingWebhook and ValidatingWebhook types. The webhook configurations are managed by configuration managers (mutating_webhook_manager.go and validating_webhook_manager.go), which expose a generic.Source interface that provides lists of WebhookAccessor instances. The webhook matching logic leverages predicate matchers in the predicates subpackages (namespace/matcher.go, object/matcher.go, rules/rules.go) to determine if a webhook should be called based on the admission request attributes. Error handling is centralized in errors/statuserror.go which converts webhook rejections into appropriate status errors. The entire chain supports advanced features like reinvocation for mutating webhooks (via mutating/reinvocationcontext.go), parallel execution for validating webhooks, timeout handling, and detailed audit annotations for webhook invocations.\"\n}\n",

admission webhook chain is implemented across multiple Go packages that work together to handle dynamic admission control for API requests. The chain begins with the main Webhook handler in generic/webhook.go, which implements the core admission.Interface and orchestrates the entire webhook admission flow. When a request arrives, the Dispatch() method in generic/webhook.go coordinates with ShouldCallHook() to determine which webhooks should be invoked based on namespace selectors, object selectors, and resource rules. The actual webhook invocations are delegated to specialized Dispatcher implementations in the mutating and validating subpackages. For mutating webhooks, the mutatingDispatcher in mutating/dispatcher.go iterates through eligible webhooks and calls callAttrMutatingHook() for each one, which handles the HTTP request/response cycle, patch application, and reinvocation logic for consecutive mutations. The validatingDispatcher in validating/dispatcher.go runs validating webhooks in parallel (via goroutines) and aggregates their responses. Both dispatchers use the request/admissionreview.go utilities to create AdmissionReview objects via CreateAdmissionObjects() and validate responses via VerifyAdmissionResponse(). The WebhookAccessor interface (defined in accessors.go) provides a unified way to access webhook configuration details for both MutatingWebhook and ValidatingWebhook types. The webhook configurations are managed by configuration managers (mutating_webhook_manager.go and validating_webhook_manager.go), which expose a generic.Source interface that provides lists of WebhookAccessor instances. The webhook matching logic leverages predicate matchers in the predicates subpackages (namespace/matcher.go, object/matcher.go, rules/rules.go) to determine if a webhook should be called based on the admission request attributes. Error handling is centralized in errors/statuserror.go which converts webhook rejections into appropriate status errors. The entire chain supports advanced features like reinvocation for mutating webhooks (via mutating/reinvocationcontext.go), parallel execution for validating webhooks, timeout handling, and detailed audit annotations for webhook invocations.\"\n}\n",
